## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration determined by position x, velocity v, and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard state-space form of (non)linear oscillators. Common governing structures include nonlinear restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and external/parametric forcing (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (small-amplitude mass-spring-damper, sign of c0 typically negative for restoring)
- Undamped conservative oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (Hookean restoring force only; energy approximately conserved)
- Simple pendulum (small-to-large angle via sine): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (gravitational restoring torque mapped to angular displacement)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring with linear damping)
- Higher-order stiffness nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (strongly nonlinear springs / beam mid-plane stretching)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic drag): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-type damping or velocity-squared losses)
- Coulomb + viscous friction model: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sign(v) (dry friction with linear damping; piecewise dynamics)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillation and limit cycles)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent self-excitation): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (limit-cycle oscillator with nonlinear damping in v)
- Driven nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (periodic forcing, resonance/chaos in Duffing-type systems)
- Driven oscillator with multiple harmonics: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) + c4 * sin(c5 * t) (multi-tone excitation / waveform forcing)
- Parametrically excited oscillator (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric resonance)
- Nonlinear restoring from potential gradient: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) + c3 * v (explicit sign convention emphasizing dv_dt = -dU/dx + damping)
- Saturating restoring force (bounded stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * tanh(c1 * x) + c2 * v (softening spring with asymptotic force limit)
- Time-modulated damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * v (periodically varying dissipation, can induce/enhance resonance)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative mechanics signature: dv_dt depends mainly on x (and is approximately odd in x), while explicit v-dependence indicates dissipation or self-excitation.
- Restoring-force symmetry: odd-polynomial in x (x, x**3, x**5) often models symmetric potentials; inclusion of even powers (x**2, x**4) suggests asymmetry or bias.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: positive cubic term with restoring sign yields frequency increasing with amplitude (hardening); negative cubic yields decreasing frequency (softening).
- Dry friction behavior: sign(v) terms create stick–slip and non-smooth trajectories; expect piecewise-linear acceleration with discontinuity at v = 0.
- Quadratic drag behavior: v*Abs(v) produces stronger damping at high speed and weak damping near v = 0; leads to amplitude-dependent decay rates.
- Self-excited oscillations: factors like (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v imply negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, yielding stable limit cycles.
- External forcing identification: additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms in dv_dt indicate driven oscillations and resonance peaks at specific frequencies.
- Parametric resonance identification: coefficients multiplying x (or v) that are periodic in t, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, indicate Mathieu-like instability regions.
- Potential-gradient structure: if dv_dt can be written as -dU/dx + D(x,v,t), then U(x) shapes equilibrium points (multiple wells if x**3 and x**5 present) and D captures damping/forcing.
- Non-smooth or bounded forces: tanh(c*x) or other sigmoids in x indicate force saturation (e.g., geometric constraints or actuator limits) and can clamp acceleration at large |x|.

**36.** Rational terms in \((c1 v+c2)\) plus \(c6*x^{c7}|v|^{c8}\).  
To remove all rational dependence, set \(c0=c3=c4=c5=0\). Then need \(c6 x^{c7}|v|^{c8}\) to equal the whole GT, impossible because GT is a *sum* of three different monomials (\(x\), \(x^3\), \(x|v|^{1/3}\)), not a single separable monomial. Alternatively keep rational terms: they introduce denominators depending on \(v\), which GT does not have. No parameter choice makes the entire expression exactly GT for all \(x,v\). **No match.**

**37.** Similar issue: has \(x/(c1 v+c2)\) etc plus one monomial \(c6 x^{c7}|v|^{c8}\) and one free \(c3 x^3\). Denominator dependence on \(v\) cannot be eliminated except by zeroing those terms, leaving at most \(x^3 + x^{c7}|v|^{c8}\), still cannot produce simultaneously \(x\) and \(x|v|^{1/3}\) and \(x^3\) unless \(c7=1,c8=1/3\) gives \(x|v|^{1/3}\), but then still missing the plain \(x\) term. Could we get plain \(x\) from the rational part? Only if denominator is constant: set \(c1=0\) so denom \(=c2\) constant. Then the rational terms become constants times \(x\), \(vx\), \(vx^3\). To avoid \(vx\) and \(vx^3\) set \(c4=c5=0\). Then we can get an \(x\) term from \(c0*x/c2\) and an \(x^3\) term from \(c3*x^3\), and \(x|v|^{1/3}\) from \(c6 x^{c7}|v|^{c8}\) with \(c7=1,c8=1/3\). This actually can match GT by choosing:
- \(c1=0\), \(c2\neq 0\)
- \(c4=0,c5=0\)
- \(c3=A\)
- \(c0/c2 = A\)  (so \(c0=A c2\))
- \(c6 = A\gamma\), \(c7=1\), \(c8=1/3\)  
All extra terms removed. **Matches.**

**38.** \(c0*x + c1*x^3 + c2*x|v|^{1/3} + c3*x*(c4+v)^{c5}\)  
Set \(c3=0\). Then match \(c1,c0,c2\). **Matches.**

**39.** \(c0*x + c1*x^3 + c2*x|v|^{1/3} + c3*v*(c4+x)^{c5}\)

**55.** All terms divided by \((c1 v+c2)\).  
If \(c1\neq 0\), unavoidable \(v\)-dependent denominator not in GT. Set \(c1=0\) so denom is constant \(c2\neq 0\). Then expression becomes a linear combination of \(x, x|v|^{1/3}, v x|v|^{1/3}, x^3, v x, v x^3\) all scaled by \(1/c2\). To match GT, set coefficients of \(v x\), \(v x^3\), and \(v x|v|^{1/3}\) to zero: \(c4=c6=c7=0\). Then we have \((c0/c2)x + (c5/c2)x^3 + (c3/c2)x|v|^{1/3}\). Choose \(c0/c2=A,\;c5/c2=A,\;c3/c2=A\gamma\). **Matches.**
